import os
from pathlib import Path

# 1) ROOT ê²°ì •: env > settings.yaml(paths.root) > ë§ˆì§€ë§‰ ì•ˆì „ ê¸°ë³¸ê°’
def _resolve_root() -> Path:

    if env:
        return Path(env)
    # ì„ íƒ: settings.yaml íŒŒì‹± (í•„ìš” ì‹œ í™œì„±í™”)
    # try:
    #     import yaml
    #     cfg = yaml.safe_load(Path("configs/settings.yaml").read_text(encoding="utf-8"))

    # ìµœí›„ì˜ ë³´ë£¨: ì‹œìŠ¤í…œ ê³ ì • ë£¨íŠ¸(ë¬¸ì„œ ê¸°ì¤€). ê·¸ë˜ë„ ì—¬ê¸° í•˜ë‚˜ë§Œ í—ˆìš©.

ROOT: Path = _resolve_root()

def P(*parts: str) -> Path:
    """ROOT ê¸°ì¤€ ìƒëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ í•©ì„±"""
    return ROOT.joinpath(*parts).resolve()

def ensure_dirs(*rel_dirs: str) -> None:
    for d in rel_dirs:
        P(d).mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

# scripts/check_velos_tasks.ps1
(Get-Content "C:\giwanos\scripts\check_velos_tasks.ps1" -Raw) `
-replace 'C:\\giwanos', '$(if ($env:VELOS_ROOT) { $env:VELOS_ROOT } else { "C:\giwanos" })' `
| Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 "C:\giwanos\scripts\check_velos_tasks.ps1"

# scripts/gpt_code_guard.ps1
(Get-Content "C:\giwanos\scripts\gpt_code_guard.ps1" -Raw) `
-replace 'C:\\giwanos', '$(if ($env:VELOS_ROOT) { $env:VELOS_ROOT } else { "C:\giwanos" })' `
| Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 "C:\giwanos\scripts\gpt_code_guard.ps1"

# scripts/log_rotate.ps1
(Get-Content "C:\giwanos\scripts\log_rotate.ps1" -Raw) `
-replace 'C:\\giwanos\\data\\logs', '$(Join-Path $(if ($env:VELOS_ROOT) { $env:VELOS_ROOT } else { "C:\giwanos" }) "data\logs")' `
| Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 "C:\giwanos\scripts\log_rotate.ps1"

# scripts/start_velos_bridge.ps1
(Get-Content "C:\giwanos\scripts\start_velos_bridge.ps1" -Raw) `
-replace 'C:\\giwanos', '$(if ($env:VELOS_ROOT) { $env:VELOS_ROOT } else { "C:\giwanos" })' `
-replace 'C:\\Users\\User\\venvs\\velos\\Scripts\\python\.exe', '$(if ($env:VELOS_PYTHON) { $env:VELOS_PYTHON } else { "python" })' `
| Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 "C:\giwanos\scripts\start_velos_bridge.ps1"

# scripts/velos_pipeline_check.ps1
(Get-Content "C:\giwanos\scripts\velos_pipeline_check.ps1" -Raw) `
-replace 'C:\\Users\\User\\venvs\\velos\\Scripts\\python\.exe', '$(if ($env:VELOS_PYTHON) { $env:VELOS_PYTHON } else { "python" })' `
| Set-Content -Encoding UTF8 "C:\giwanos\scripts\velos_pipeline_check.ps1"

# ë¡œí…Œì´ì…˜ ì²˜ë¦¬
foreach ($ext in $extensions) {
    Get-ChildItem -Path $logDir -Filter $ext -File -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue | ForEach-Object {
        try {
            $dest = Join-Path $backupDir "$($_.BaseName)_$dateStamp$($_.Extension)"
            Move-Item -Path $_.FullName -Destination $dest -Force
            Write-Host "âœ… ë¡œí…Œì´ì…˜ ì™„ë£Œ: $($_.Name) â†’ $(Split-Path $dest -Leaf)"
        }
        catch {
            Write-Host "âš  ë¡œí…Œì´ì…˜ ì‹¤íŒ¨: $($_.FullName) - $($_.Exception.Message)"
        }
    }
}

# ë ˆí¬ ë£¨íŠ¸ì—ì„œ ì‹¤í–‰ (Windows PowerShell)

@'
#!/usr/bin/env pwsh
$ErrorActionPreference = "Stop"
$patterns = @("([A-Z]:\\)")   # ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ íŒ¨í„´
$files = git diff --cached --name-only --diff-filter=ACMRT | Where-Object {
  $_ -match '\.(py|ps1)$'
}
$bad = @()
foreach ($f in $files) {
  foreach ($p in $patterns) {
    $m = Select-String -Path $f -Pattern $p -AllMatches -SimpleMatch:$false -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue
    if ($m) { $bad += $m }
  }
}
if ($bad.Count -gt 0) {
  Write-Host "`nâŒ í•˜ë“œì½”ë”© ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ë°œê²¬. ì»¤ë°‹ ì°¨ë‹¨:" -ForegroundColor Red
  $bad | ForEach-Object { Write-Host "$($_.Path):$($_.LineNumber):$($_.Line.Trim())" }
  Write-Host "`nğŸ‘‰ VELOS ê·œì¹™: í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ VELOS_ROOT ë˜ëŠ” report_paths ëª¨ë“ˆë§Œ ì‚¬ìš©." -ForegroundColor Yellow
  exit 1
}
exit 0

tests/test_no_hardcoded_paths.py

import re, pathlib

PATTERN = re.compile(r"([A-Z]:\\)")
ALLOWLIST = {
    # ì£¼ì„ ì „ìš© íŒŒì¼ ë“± ê¼­ í—ˆìš©í•  ê²Œ ìˆìœ¼ë©´ ì—¬ê¸°ì— ì¶”ê°€
}

def iter_files(root="."):
    exts = (".py", ".ps1")
    for p in pathlib.Path(root).rglob("*"):
        if p.suffix.lower() in exts and p.is_file():
            yield p

def test_no_windows_abs_paths():
    offenders = []
    for p in iter_files():
        if str(p) in ALLOWLIST: 
            continue
        for i, line in enumerate(p.read_text(encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore").splitlines(), 1):
            if PATTERN.search(line):
                offenders.append(f"{p}:{i}:{line.strip()}")
    if offenders:
        raise AssertionError("Hardcoded paths found:\n" + "\n".join(offenders))

import re, sys
from pathlib import Path

def _scan_repo_for_abs():
    pat = re.compile(r"([A-Z]:\\)")
    root = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[1]
    offenders = []
    for p in root.rglob("*"):
        if p.suffix.lower() in {".py", ".ps1"} and p.is_file():
            for i, line in enumerate(p.read_text("utf-8", errors="ignore").splitlines(), 1):
                if pat.search(line):
                    offenders.append(f"{p}:{i}:{line.strip()}")
    if offenders:
        raise SystemExit("Hardcoded paths found:\n" + "\n".join(offenders))
# í•„ìš”í•  ë•Œë§Œ ì¼œê³ , í‰ì†Œì—” í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ë¡œ ë¹„í™œì„±í™”

Integrating GPT-5 with Cursor AI: Automated Bidirectional Workflows

Integrating OpenAIâ€™s GPT-5 with the Cursor AI code editor can create a powerful feedback loop: GPT-5 can generate code or designs which Cursor executes/refines, and Cursorâ€™s code edits can be sent back to GPT-5 for analysis or improvement. Below, we explore multiple integration methods â€“ from GitHub-based CI pipelines to multi-agent frameworks â€“ and discuss their workflows, pros, and cons. Each approach includes practical steps for implementation in a development setting.

1. GitHub-Based Workflow Integration (Triggers & Actions)

One straightforward approach is leveraging GitHub as the integration hub. You can use GitHub pull request triggers, comments, and Actions workflows to pass code between GPT-5 and Cursor:

Pull Request Comment Triggers: Cursor offers a GitHub App integration that allows background agents to act on repository events. By installing the Cursor GitHub app and giving it access, you can simply comment @cursor <prompt> on a PR or issue to trigger an AI agent. For example, commenting @cursor fix on a PR can instruct Cursorâ€™s agent to apply a suggested fix from its code review (Bugbot) and push a commit
docs.cursor.com
. This lets GPT-powered agents respond to human prompts directly on GitHub, reading the code context from the PR and committing changes via the app.

GitHub Actions Pipeline: For more customized automation, set up a CI workflow that calls GPT-5 and Cursor in sequence. Using Cursorâ€™s CLI in a GitHub Action, the workflow might: (1) check out the repo on a push/PR event; (2) run GPT-5 (via Cursor CLI or OpenAI API) to generate or modify code; (3) run tests or lint; (4) possibly call GPT-5 again for analysis; and (5) commit or comment results. An example from an OpenAPI generation workflow shows installing Cursor CLI in CI, then invoking cursor-agent with GPT-5 to generate a file, followed by test and deployment steps
apidog.com
apidog.com
. In that pipeline, the Cursor CLI is used headlessly with -m gpt-5 -p "<prompt>", and its output is redirected to a file (or could be a diff/patch)
apidog.com
. This demonstrates that GPT-5 can be run via Cursor CLI in an automated fashion, with Cursor acting as the code generator in CI. After generation, you could add a step to run Cursorâ€™s agent again to, say, fix any lint/test issues (or use @cursor fix in a PR comment to trigger an agent to address CI failures).

Workflow Example (GitHub Actions):

Developer Push/PR â€“ Developer prompts GPT-5 for a feature or commits initial code. This triggers a CI workflow (on push or PR creation).

GPT-5 Code Generation â€“ The CI job calls GPT-5 (via API or Cursor CLI) to generate or update code. For instance, using Cursor CLI in non-interactive mode: cursor-agent -m gpt-5 -p "Implement feature X..." --print will apply changes or output proposed code
apidog.com
. The agent can be granted write access to directly modify the repository in the CI runner
docs.cursor.com
.

Cursor Agent Execution â€“ The CI workflow (or a PR comment) triggers Cursorâ€™s agent to run any tests or refinements. For example, you might include a command in the prompt like â€œrun tests after applyingâ€ â€“ Cursorâ€™s agent can execute shell commands such as npm test after editing code
apidog.com
. In a GitHub comment scenario, the Cursor background agent can clone the repo, make changes, and push a new commit automatically
docs.cursor.com
.

Feedback to GPT-5 â€“ Results (like test outcomes or diff of changes) are fed back. This could be done by a follow-up GitHub Action step that calls GPT-5â€™s API to analyze the test results or review the diff. Some projects use Actions to have GPT-4/GPT-5 comment on PRs with a code review
cookbook.openai.com
, which can be extended to reviewing Cursorâ€™s modifications.

Iteration or Approval â€“ Optionally, the process can loop: GPT-5 suggests fixes for failing tests, commits, Cursor runs again, etc., until CI passes. Finally, a human developer reviews the PR with all AI-made commits.

Pros: This method keeps all changes version-controlled and visible. GitHubâ€™s triggers provide a structured, auditable workflow. Teams can leverage familiar PR reviews and require human approval before merging AI-generated changes. The Cursor GitHub integration in particular allows on-demand agent assistance by simply commenting on issues/PRs, which is very convenient
docs.cursor.com
. Using GitHub Actions offers flexibility: you can integrate testing, deployment, and even other tools (as shown in the OpenAPI CI example) in one automated pipeline
apidog.com
. Secrets (API keys) are managed by GitHub, and the whole team sees the history of AI interventions in Git history.

 

Cons: GitHub-based integration can be slower due to the push/CI cycle latency. Itâ€™s not real-time; each iteration might require a commit or comment and waiting for the action to complete. Setting up the CI workflow or Cursorâ€™s GitHub app requires some initial configuration (API keys, permissions, etc.). Also, fully autonomous loops should be used with caution â€“ itâ€™s wise to include manual checks (e.g., require an approval before auto-merging) because blindly committing AI changes could introduce errors
apidog.com
. Thereâ€™s also a limit to context: large codebases might exceed prompt limits, so you may need to enable Cursorâ€™s indexing or chunking of the code in the agentâ€™s prompt (which the Cursor app can do via its codebase index) â€“ in CI youâ€™d have to manage providing necessary context to GPT-5.

2. Direct API & CLI Integration (Scripting Approach)

Another approach is to write a custom script or tool that directly connects GPT-5â€™s API and Cursorâ€™s CLI/SDK, enabling back-and-forth outside of GitHub. This is more free-form and can run in any environment (local machine, a server, or even as a part of an IDE plugin).

 

Workflow Example (Scripted Automation):

Step 1: GPT-5 Generates Code â€“ Your script calls the OpenAI GPT-5 API (assuming you have access) with a prompt to produce code or a design. For example, using OpenAIâ€™s Python SDK, the script might send the prompt â€œWrite a Python function for Xâ€ and get back code.

Step 2: Feed to Cursor for Execution/Refinement â€“ The script then invokes Cursor via its CLI or API. The Cursor CLI (cursor-agent) can be run in non-interactive â€œprintâ€ mode for automation
docs.cursor.com
. You could save GPT-5â€™s code to a file and ask Cursor to review or modify it: e.g. cursor-agent -p "Optimize the code in file.py and fix any bugs" --output-format text. Because the CLI has full write access in non-interactive mode
docs.cursor.com
, the Cursor agent can directly edit the files or run them. You might also instruct Cursorâ€™s agent to run the code or tests by including a command in the prompt (the agentâ€™s toolkit allows shell commands)
docs.cursor.com
apidog.com
. If preferred, use --output-format json to get structured output (like a JSON patch or a list of changes) for the script to parse
docs.cursor.com
.

Step 3: Return Results to GPT-5 â€“ After Cursor executes, gather the results. This could be program output, error messages, or a diff of what Cursor changed. The script then calls GPT-5 API again, supplying those results in the prompt for analysis or improvement suggestions. For instance, â€œHere is the error log from running the code, please debug it.â€ GPT-5 would analyze and produce a fix or explanation.

Step 4: Iterate or Finalize â€“ The script can loop back: apply GPT-5â€™s fixes (possibly via Cursor again), and repeat until no errors remain. Finally, the combined result can be presented or stored.

Pros: This method offers fine-grained control. You can orchestrate each step exactly â€“ choosing when to invoke GPT-5 vs Cursor â€“ and inject custom logic (e.g., only call GPT-5 if an error occurred, etc.). It doesnâ€™t rely on any specific platform except the APIs/CLI, so you can run it locally or on a custom CI server. The Cursor CLI is built to be script-friendly (headless usage) and can incorporate your projectâ€™s context (via rules or an AGENT.md for guidance) just as the Cursor IDE would
docs.cursor.com
docs.cursor.com
. Also, since itâ€™s code, you can integrate other tools; for example, after Cursor runs, your script might also run a static analyzer, then ask GPT-5 to address any issues it reports.

 

Cons: Youâ€™ll need to write and maintain the orchestration code, which can get complex. Handling the state between GPT-5 and Cursor is up to you â€“ you might have to save files or conversation context manually. Unlike the GitHub approach, thereâ€™s no built-in review interface; youâ€™d need to log outputs or diffs for a human to inspect. Error handling is critical (e.g., if GPT-5 output is not syntactically correct, or Cursorâ€™s tool actions fail). Moreover, calling GPT-5 via API and running Cursor CLI requires managing API keys and environment security (the Cursor CLI can run arbitrary shell commands, so only run it in a safe environment)
apidog.com
. Another limitation is stateful conversation: GPT-5 via API doesnâ€™t automatically know what Cursor did unless you feed it that info. You might need to maintain a conversation memory in the script (e.g., include previous messages in the prompt) to give GPT-5 context across turns. This is doable, but careful token management is needed to stay within GPT-5â€™s context window.

3. Multi-Agent Framework Integration (LangChain, AutoGen, CrewAI, etc.)

For a higher-level solution, you can use emerging multi-agent frameworks like LangChain (with agents), Microsoft AutoGen, or CrewAI to coordinate GPT-5 and Cursor in a conversational loop. These frameworks let you define multiple AI â€œagentsâ€ with distinct roles and facilitate complex back-and-forth workflows automatically
medium.com
.

 

Approach: Define one agent as a â€œCoderâ€ (leveraging GPT-5â€™s coding ability) and another as an â€œExecutor/Editorâ€ (which uses Cursor or some tool to run and modify code). The agents can pass messages or tasks to each other. For example, using AutoGen, you might create an â€œAutomated Debugging Squadâ€: one agent reads error logs, another searches documentation, and a third generates bug fixes
medium.com
. In the context of GPT-5 + Cursor, the pattern could be:

Coder Agent (GPT-5): Receives a task (e.g., â€œimplement feature Xâ€), writes code for it and sends the code to the next agent.

Executor Agent (Cursor): Receives the code, inserts it into the project, runs it or executes tests using Cursorâ€™s tools, and returns the results (e.g. error output or success confirmation) to the coder agent.

Reviewer Agent (GPT-5): (Optional) A third agent could evaluate the Executorâ€™s output (e.g., does the code style meet guidelines? Are there potential edge cases unhandled?) and provide feedback or improvements. This could loop back to the Coder agent for adjustments.

Frameworks like LangChain can implement such an interaction by giving an LLM agent access to tools â€“ one tool could be a â€œRun codeâ€ tool (which under the hood uses the Cursor CLI or a Python REPL), another tool could be a â€œRead fileâ€ or â€œWrite fileâ€ operation. The GPT-5 agent can decide to call these tools and then get the output, simulating what Cursor does but orchestrated by the agentâ€™s reasoning. On the other hand, AutoGen natively supports multi-turn dialogues between independent agents. It allows each agent to have a persona and memory, so the coder and tester agents can remember past exchanges and gradually refine the solution
medium.com
medium.com
. CrewAI takes a role-based approach â€“ you explicitly define agents like â€œFrontendDevâ€, â€œBackendDevâ€, â€œTesterâ€, each with specific responsibilities and tools, then let the framework coordinate their collaboration
medium.com
medium.com
. CrewAI emphasizes a structured team-like delegation (one agent can hand off a subtask to another), which could be ideal if you want a deterministic pipeline (e.g., always code -> then test -> then review, with agents specialized in each).

 

Pros: These frameworks provide out-of-the-box structure for complex interactions. They handle message passing, keeping context, and sometimes even logging or monitoring the conversation between agents. This can dramatically reduce the amount of glue code you have to write â€“ you declare the roles and tools, and the framework manages the loop of one agentâ€™s output becoming anotherâ€™s input. For instance, AutoGen is designed for dynamic collaboration where agents can even reassign tasks or self-correct over multiple turns
medium.com
. Such capabilities can lead to more resilient workflows (e.g., if the code fails, the agents might automatically try different fixes). These frameworks also often integrate memory (so agents recall prior steps) and allow plugging in evaluation or guardrails (to stop if a criterion is met or a risk detected). Another benefit is scalability: you could run these agents asynchronously or in parallel for different parts of a large project, since frameworks like CrewAI are built for enterprise scaling with many agents and tasks
medium.com
medium.com
.

 

Cons: Multi-agent systems add complexity and are still a cutting-edge area. Setting up AutoGen or CrewAI requires learning their APIs and designing prompts/roles carefully. They can be resource-intensive (multiple GPT-5 calls in a loop can consume a lot of tokens quickly)
medium.com
. Debugging a multi-agent conversation can be non-trivial â€“ you might encounter situations where agents go in circles or produce unexpected outputs. Itâ€™s important to constrain agents with proper prompts or rules (for example, limit how many iterations or have a supervisor agent to decide when to stop). Additionally, connecting these frameworks to Cursor might require writing a custom tool wrapper. For example, in LangChain youâ€™d implement a tool that calls cursor-agent under the hood. In CrewAI or AutoGen, you might integrate Cursor via its MCP (Model Context Protocol) interface if supported (Cursor CLI and Cursor IDE support MCP for extending functionality
docs.cursor.com
, and CrewAI has an MCP integration module
docs.crewai.com
). This adds an extra integration step. Lastly, not all frameworks may directly support interactive approval â€“ if your Cursor agent needs to run shell commands, you must ensure the framework can handle an interactive step or you run Cursor in an auto-approve mode for commands. Despite these challenges, success is possible: for instance, CrewAIâ€™s documentation and community examples demonstrate coding agents that generate and execute code, even integrating an â€œOpen Interpreterâ€ to run code and feed results back into the agents
youtube.com
workos.com
.

4. Unified Local Environment Integration

This approach tries to run GPT-5 and Cursor in the same environment (machine or development space) to make the exchange of information seamless. The idea is that if both the LLM and Cursor share access to the same files, processes, or memory, you can reduce friction in passing data back and forth.

 

Scenario: You have a development VM or local machine where youâ€™ve installed Cursor (CLI or the Cursor IDE) and you also have access to GPT-5 (either via API or a local model). Both are configured to work on the same project directory. This way, any code generated by GPT-5 can immediately be put into the files that Cursor can see, and any edits or execution results from Cursor can be read by GPT-5.

 

How to Implement: One way is to use Cursor CLIâ€™s session features and OpenAIâ€™s API together. For example, you might start a Cursor CLI session in one process (which keeps an agent running with context), and programmatically send instructions to it. At the same time, maintain a GPT-5 conversation in your script. If the two processes can communicate via files or network calls, you can do something like: GPT-5â€™s response is written to a file or a queue; Cursor CLI (running in a loop reading that file) picks it up and executes; Cursor then writes results (maybe to a log file or as a CLI output) which the GPT-5 process then reads and incorporates into its next prompt. This could even be done within a single Python script using threading: one thread calls GPT-5 API, another runs cursor-agent commands (via subprocess calls or using Cursorâ€™s Python API if provided). Because the environment is shared, GPT-5 doesnâ€™t need to rely solely on token context for code â€“ the script can feed entire files or paths to GPT-5 from disk, and Cursor naturally operates on the actual files.

 

Alternatively, if GPT-5 were available as a local model (hypothetically, say an open-source model fine-tuned to GPT-5 level), you could integrate at an even lower level â€“ possibly plugging that model into Cursor as a custom model. (Cursorâ€™s design allows choosing models like GPT-4, Claude, and presumably could allow a local endpoint via their â€œmodelâ€ parameter or MCP servers
docs.cursor.com
cursor.com
.) Running both under one roof (for example, self-hosting an LLM and running Cursorâ€™s index and tools on the same server) could allow state sharing like a common vector database for code embeddings, etc., though this is an advanced setup.

 

Pros: Keeping everything in one environment can make the integration faster and more private. Thereâ€™s less overhead in transferring data (no need to push to GitHub or call out to external CI each time). Itâ€™s ideal for rapid prototyping: you could essentially mimic what ChatGPTâ€™s Code Interpreter plugin does (generate code -> run code -> get output) entirely on your machine. Because Cursor CLI can be driven from the terminal, a savvy developer could even create a local TUI or script that shows GPTâ€™s suggestions and applies them with Cursor in real-time. Shared local state also means you can use local caches or memory â€“ for instance, store intermediate results on disk and have both GPT-5 and Cursor read it as needed, avoiding hitting context length limits for large data. Another benefit is that if everything is local (especially if using a local LLM), you are not sending potentially sensitive code to an external service â€“ this could appeal for highly secure environments.

 

Cons: Running GPT-5 locally is generally not feasible unless OpenAI releases an on-prem model or you use an approximation; most likely youâ€™ll still be calling an API, so â€œunified environmentâ€ primarily helps with file sharing but not with eliminating external calls. Orchestration is still needed (similar to method 2), itâ€™s just that it all happens on one machine. This method can become essentially a custom implementation of an agent loop, so it inherits many of the same challenges as the scripting approach (error handling, ensuring the two systems stay in sync, etc.). Without GitHub or a framework, you also donâ€™t have a built-in logging of what happened, so youâ€™ll want to implement good logging yourself to trace the changes made by the AI. Another limitation is that Cursorâ€™s state (like its conversation or index) in the CLI might not be easily exposed to GPT-5 â€“ you may still have to explicitly pass any relevant info. For example, if Cursorâ€™s agent identified and fixed 3 bugs, GPT-5 wouldnâ€™t â€œknowâ€ that unless you feed it a summary or diff. Essentially, shared environment makes it easier to share data (files, outputs) but not the internal reasoning state of the agents â€“ that remains siloed unless bridged by your code. Finally, consider resource use: running Cursor (which uses GPT models internally) and GPT-5 calls simultaneously could be heavy on a single machine; careful orchestration or sequential operation might be needed to avoid contention.

5. Limitations and Considerations

Regardless of the integration method, there are important limitations and best practices to keep in mind:

API Access & Costs: As of 2025, GPT-5 access might be limited. In Cursor, GPT-5 is available (they enabled it for users during launch week)
cursor.com
, but using it via API could be costly. Both GPT-5 and Cursorâ€™s services may have rate limits. For heavy workflows (e.g. multi-agent loops or large CI jobs), monitor usage to avoid hitting quotas or incurring unexpected costs. You might use smaller models for intermediate steps if appropriate (Cursor supports selecting different models via --model flag
apidog.com
).

Context Length & Code Size: Large codebases pose a challenge â€“ even GPT-5 has context limits. Cursor partially addresses this with code indexing and the ability to fetch relevant code snippets for the prompt
docs.cursor.com
, but when automating, you must ensure important context (dependency code, config files, etc.) is provided. One strategy is to use Cursorâ€™s â€œmemoriesâ€ or â€œrulesâ€ features to inject domain knowledge to the agent
docs.cursor.com
. If using an external GPT API, you might chunk code or have GPT-5 summarize parts of the codebase first. Thereâ€™s a trade-off between giving the AI full context (which might be too large) versus letting it operate in smaller scope and potentially missing cross-file issues.

Reliability of AI-Generated Code: AI can produce errors or non-optimal code. Integration doesnâ€™t eliminate the need for testing and validation. In fact, you should automate the safety nets: always run the test suite after AI makes changes, and consider using static analysis or type-checking as additional steps. The Apidog example showed how even with GPT-5, the output might need re-running with adjusted prompts (e.g., GPT-5 initially added unwanted text around a YAML, requiring a stricter prompt on retry)
apidog.com
. Having loops or checks to catch these failure modes is crucial for a robust pipeline.

Tool Execution Limits: Cursorâ€™s agent can run shell commands and edit files, which is powerful but dangerous. By default, the CLI asks for approval before executing commands when in interactive mode
docs.cursor.com
. In non-interactive mode it assumes you trust it and runs with full write access
docs.cursor.com
. This means an automated Cursor agent could potentially execute any code â€“ a misprompted agent might, say, try to install a package or delete a file. Always run such automation in a sandbox or CI runner thatâ€™s isolated. For production scenarios, the principle of least privilege is key: do not give the agent credentials or access it doesnâ€™t absolutely need, and consider forcing a human checkpoint for destructive actions
apidog.com
. For example, you could require manual review of a pull request that the agent proposes, rather than auto-merging it.

Session and State Sharing: GPT-5 and Cursor do not share state inherently â€“ you have to pass information between them. Plan how to summarize Cursorâ€™s actions for GPT-5 input. This could be as simple as taking a git diff of Cursorâ€™s commit and asking GPT-5 â€œReview these changes for any issues.â€ (Cursor CLI even has an example of reviewing changes for security issues with a prompt
docs.cursor.com
). Likewise, if GPT-5 has a plan or design rationale, you might record that (in a file or issue description) so that Cursorâ€™s agent can reference it. The integration is not magically â€œmind-meldedâ€; itâ€™s about structured communication between two AI-driven components.

Multi-Agent Complexity: If using frameworks like AutoGen or CrewAI, be mindful of their current maturity. They add overhead and may require tuning conversation prompts to keep agents on track. CrewAI focuses on well-defined roles which can simplify some interactions (each agent knows its job)
medium.com
, but you have to implement the roles for coding tasks (e.g., a â€œSenior Developerâ€ agent with code execution permission
medium.com
). AutoGen allows more free-form discussion which is powerful but could go off-topic if not constrained
medium.com
. Itâ€™s often useful to implement a timeout or max iterations to avoid infinite loops between agents arguing or redoing tasks endlessly.

Human Oversight: No matter the automation, keeping a human in the loop is wise, especially for critical code. For instance, Cursorâ€™s â€œBugbotâ€ can suggest PR fixes, but typically a human reviews the suggestions; even if you auto-apply them with @cursor fix, treat the resulting PR as you would a junior developerâ€™s commit â€“ do a final review. The goal of integration is to accelerate development, not to remove humans entirely from the process. A practical tip is to log all AI decisions (in commit messages, PR comments, or a separate log file) so you can trace why a certain change was made.

In summary, automating GPT-5 â†” Cursor AI integration can be achieved via multiple pathways. A GitHub-centric workflow is great for leveraging existing CI/CD and collaborative practices
apidog.com
, while direct scripting or multi-agent systems offer flexibility and cutting-edge capabilities
medium.com
medium.com
. Itâ€™s even possible to run both tools in tandem on a single machine for fast feedback loops. Each method comes with trade-offs in complexity, speed, and safety. By combining these approaches with robust testing and oversight, developers can create a development loop where GPT-5â€™s intelligence and Cursorâ€™s coding automation complement each other â€“ GPT-5 proposing solutions and analyses, and Cursor executing changes and validations â€“ leading to faster and smarter software development cycles.

# .github/workflows/ci.yml
name: VELOS CI
on:
  pull_request:
    branches: [ main, develop ]
jobs:
  guard-test-review:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4

      - name: Path guard (no absolute Windows paths)
        run: |
          ! grep -RInE '([A-Z]:\\\\)' --include='*.py' --include='*.ps1' . \
          || (echo "âŒ Hardcoded absolute path found"; exit 1)

      - name: Setup Python
        uses: actions/setup-python@v5
        with: { python-version: '3.11' }

      - name: Install deps & test
        run: |
          pip install -r requirements.txt || true
          pytest -q

      - name: Cursor auto-fix on fail (optional)
        if: ${{ failure() }}
        env:
          CURSOR_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.CURSOR_API_KEY }}
        run: |
          cursor-agent -p "í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ì‹¤íŒ¨ë¥¼ ìµœì†Œ ìˆ˜ì •ìœ¼ë¡œ ê³ ì³ë¼. ê·œì¹™: AGENT.md" --print || true

      - name: GPT-5 PR review summary
        if: always()
        env:
          OPENAI_API_KEY: ${{ secrets.OPENAI_API_KEY }}
        run: |
          python .github/scripts/gpt_review.py

# C:\giwanos\tools\make_context_pack.py
New-Item -ItemType Directory -Force C:\giwanos\tools | Out-Null
@'
import json, os, re
from datetime import datetime
BASE = r"C:\giwanos"
MEM = os.path.join(BASE, "data", "memory", "learning_memory.json")
RULES = os.path.join(BASE, "docs", "RULES.md")
OUT = os.path.join(BASE, "docs", "CONTEXT_PACK.md")

def tail(path, n=200):
    try:
        with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
            lines = f.readlines()
        return lines[-n:]
    except FileNotFoundError:
        return []

def extract_highlights(lines):
    out=[]
    for ln in lines:
        try:
            j = json.loads(ln.strip())
            txt = j.get("insight","")
            if any(k in txt for k in ["ê²½ë¡œ","VELOS_ROOT","í•˜ë“œì½”ë”©","ê·œì¹™","ëª©í‘œ","ì¤‘ìš”","ì£¼ì˜"]):
                out.append(f"- {txt}")
        except Exception:
            pass
    return out[-50:]  # ë„ˆë¬´ ê¸¸ë©´ ìë¦„

rules = ""
try:
    with open(RULES,"r",encoding="utf-8") as f:
        rules = f.read()
except FileNotFoundError:
    rules = "# RULES\n(ê·œì¹™ íŒŒì¼ ì—†ìŒ)"

mem_tail = tail(MEM, n=500)
hi = extract_highlights(mem_tail)

now = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
doc = []
doc.append(f"# CONTEXT PACK  ({now})")
doc.append("## í•µì‹¬ ê·œì¹™ ìš”ì•½")
doc.append(rules.strip())
doc.append("## ìµœê·¼ ë©”ëª¨ë¦¬ í•˜ì´ë¼ì´íŠ¸(ìµœëŒ€ 50)")
doc.extend(hi if hi else ["- ìµœê·¼ í•˜ì´ë¼ì´íŠ¸ ì—†ìŒ"])
doc.append("## ì‘ì—… ìƒíƒœ ì²´í¬ë¦¬ìŠ¤íŠ¸")
doc.append("- ê²½ë¡œ: VELOS_ROOT ë§Œ ì‚¬ìš©, ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ê¸ˆì§€")
doc.append("- í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ì‹¤íŒ¨ì‹œ: ìµœì†Œ ìˆ˜ì • ì›ì¹™")
doc.append("- ë³€ê²½ì€ PR ë¸Œëœì¹˜ì—ì„œë§Œ, mainì€ ë³´í˜¸")
with open(OUT,"w",encoding="utf-8") as f:
    f.write("\n\n".join(doc))
print(f"âœ… CONTEXT_PACK ìƒì„±: {OUT}")

3) ì„¸ì…˜ ë¦¬ì…‹ ê°ì§€ê¸°(SRD)

ëŒ€ë‹µì´ ë¹„ì •ìƒì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì§§ê±°ë‚˜, ìš°ë¦¬ê°€ í•­ìƒ ë“¤ì–´ìˆì–´ì•¼ í•˜ëŠ” í‚¤ì›Œë“œ(ì˜ˆ: VELOS_ROOT) ê°€ ì‚¬ë¼ì§€ë©´ â€œëŠê¹€â€ìœ¼ë¡œ ë³´ê³  CPACK ì¬ì£¼ì…ì„ ê°•ì œí•œë‹¤.

# C:\giwanos\tools\session_reset_guard.py
@'
import sys, re, subprocess, os

MIN_LEN = 300         # ì´ë³´ë‹¤ ì§§ìœ¼ë©´ ì˜ì‹¬
MUST_KEYS = ["VELOS_ROOT","ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ê¸ˆì§€","ìµœì†Œ ìˆ˜ì •","PR ë¸Œëœì¹˜"]

def needs_reinject(text):
    if len(text) < MIN_LEN: return True
    text_low = text.lower()
    miss = [k for k in MUST_KEYS if k.lower() not in text_low]
    return len(miss) >= 2

def rebuild_context_pack():
    subprocess.run(["python", r"C:\giwanos\tools\make_context_pack.py"], check=False)
    with open(r"C:\giwanos\docs\CONTEXT_PACK.md","r",encoding="utf-8") as f:
        return f.read()

def main():
    # stdinìœ¼ë¡œ GPT ì‘ë‹µì„ ë°›ëŠ”ë‹¤ê³  ê°€ì •
    text = sys.stdin.read()
    if needs_reinject(text):
        cp = rebuild_context_pack()
        sys.stdout.write("<<CONTEXT_REINJECT>>\n")
        sys.stdout.write(cp)
        sys.stdout.write("\n\n")
        sys.stdout.write("<<ORIGINAL_REPLY>>\n")
        sys.stdout.write(text)
    else:
        sys.stdout.write(text)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

param(
  [switch]$Once  # autofix 1íšŒë§Œ ì‹¤í–‰í• ì§€ ì—¬ë¶€
)
$pwsh = "C:\Program Files\PowerShell\7\pwsh.exe"
$ps   = "$env:SystemRoot\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe"

function Run-Pwsh {
  param([string]$File,[string[]]$Args)
  if (Test-Path $pwsh) {
    & $pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File $File @Args
  } else {
    & $ps   -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File $File @Args
  }
}

param(
  [string]$MemJson = "C:\giwanos\data\memory\learning_memory.json",
  [string]$ProbeTag = "[MWA_PROBE]"
)

$ErrorActionPreference = "Stop"

# íŒŒì¼/í´ë” ë³´ì¥
$dir = Split-Path $MemJson -Parent
if (-not (Test-Path $dir)) { New-Item -ItemType Directory -Force $dir | Out-Null }
if (-not (Test-Path $MemJson)) { New-Item -ItemType File -Force $MemJson | Out-Null }

$ts = (Get-Date).ToString("yyyy-MM-ddTHH:mm:ss")
$entry = @{ from="system"; insight="$ProbeTag heartbeat $ts"; ts=$ts } | ConvertTo-Json -Compress

# ì“°ê¸°
Add-Content -LiteralPath $MemJson -Value $entry

Start-Sleep -Milliseconds 200

# ì½ê¸° ê²€ì¦
$hit = Select-String -Path $MemJson -Pattern $ProbeTag -SimpleMatch -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue
if (-not $hit) {
    Write-Host "âŒ ë©”ëª¨ë¦¬ ì“°ê¸°/ì½ê¸° ì‹¤íŒ¨: $MemJson" -ForegroundColor Red
    exit 2
}
Write-Host "âœ… ë©”ëª¨ë¦¬ OK: $($hit.Count) entries (latest $ts)" -ForegroundColor Green
'@

3) C:\giwanos\tools\autofix.ps1 ë®ì–´ì“°ê¸°
Set-Content -Path "C:\giwanos\tools\autofix.ps1" -Encoding UTF8 -Value @'
param([switch]$Once)

$ErrorActionPreference = "Stop"

function Run-Tests {
    Write-Host "[autofix] pytest ì‹¤í–‰" -ForegroundColor Cyan
    $out = (& python -m pytest -q 2>&1) | Out-String
    $code = $LASTEXITCODE
    return @{ code = $code; log = $out }
}

function Have-CursorAgent {
    try { Get-Command cursor-agent -ErrorAction Stop | Out-Null; return $true } catch { return $false }
}

function Minimal-Fix([string]$log, [string]$diff) {
    if (-not (Have-CursorAgent)) {
        Write-Host "[autofix] cursor-agent ì—†ìŒ. ìë™ìˆ˜ì • ìŠ¤í‚µ" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow
        return
    }
    $prompt = @"
í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ì‹¤íŒ¨ë¥¼ ìµœì†Œ ìˆ˜ì •ìœ¼ë¡œ ê³ ì³ë¼.
ê·œì¹™: VELOS ê²½ë¡œëŠ” í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ ê¸°ë°˜(ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ê¸ˆì§€), ë³€ê²½ì€ í•„ìš”í•œ ë¶€ë¶„ë§Œ.
í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ë¡œê·¸:
$log

Diff(ê¸°ì¤€):
$diff
"@
    cursor-agent -p $prompt --print | Out-Null
}

function Commit-If-Changed {
    $changed = (git status --porcelain) | Out-String
    if ($changed.Trim().Length -gt 0) {
        git add -A
        try { git -c user.email=ci@local -c user.name=ci commit -m "autofix: minimal patch via Cursor agent" | Out-Null } catch { }
        Write-Host "[autofix] ë³€ê²½ ì»¤ë°‹" -ForegroundColor Green
    } else {
        Write-Host "[autofix] ì»¤ë°‹í•  ë³€ê²½ ì—†ìŒ" -ForegroundColor DarkGray
    }
}

# 1íšŒ ì‹¤í–‰ ë£¨í‹´
function Run-Once {
    $t = Run-Tests
    if ($t.code -ne 0) {
        $diff = (git diff --unified=0) | Out-String
        Minimal-Fix -log $t.log -diff $diff
        Commit-If-Changed
    } else {
        Write-Host "[autofix] í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ í†µê³¼" -ForegroundColor Green
    }
}

if ($Once) {
    Run-Once
    exit 0
}

# ê°ì‹œ ë£¨í”„
Write-Host "[autofix] íŒŒì¼ ë³€ê²½ ê°ì‹œ ì‹œì‘ (3ì´ˆ ê°„ê²©)" -ForegroundColor Cyan

    Start-Sleep 3
    $dirty = (git status --porcelain) | Out-String
    if ($dirty.Trim().Length -gt 0) {
        Run-Once
    }
}

ì ê¹ ë£¨í”„ ë©ˆì¶”ê¸°, 2) ë¼ì¸ ì—”ë”© ì •ë¦¬, 3) autofixê°€ â€œì»¤ë°‹í•´ë„ ë˜ëŠ” ë³€ê²½â€ë§Œ ì»¤ë°‹í•˜ë„ë¡ í•„í„°ë§.

0) ì¼ë‹¨ ê°ì‹œ ë£¨í”„ ë„ì

ì§€ê¸ˆ ë–  ìˆëŠ” ì°½ì—ì„œ Ctrl + C.

1) ë¼ì¸ ì—”ë”© ì •ì±… ê³ ì •(.gitattributes) + ë¯¼ê° ê²½ë¡œ ë¬´ì‹œ(.gitignore)
# .gitattributes: íŒŒì¼ íƒ€ì…ë³„ ë¼ì¸ ì—”ë”© ê³ ì •
Set-Content -Path ".gitattributes" -Encoding UTF8 -Value @'
# í…ìŠ¤íŠ¸ ìë™ ì •ê·œí™”
* text=auto

# íŒŒì´ì¬/ì…¸/ìœ ë‹‰ìŠ¤ ìŠ¤í¬ë¦½íŠ¸ëŠ” LF
*.py  text eol=lf
*.sh  text eol=lf
*.md  text eol=lf
*.json text eol=lf
*.yaml text eol=lf
*.yml text eol=lf

# íŒŒì›Œì…€/ë°°ì¹˜/ìœˆë„ ìŠ¤í¬ë¦½íŠ¸ëŠ” CRLF
*.ps1 text eol=crlf
*.bat text eol=crlf

# ë°”ì´ë„ˆë¦¬
*.db  binary
*.png binary
*.jpg binary

'@

# .gitignore: ì‹œí¬ë¦¿/ë°±ì—…/ì‚°ì¶œë¬¼ ë¬´ì‹œ

# secrets
configs/.env

# backups

# runtime artifacts
data/memory/learning_memory.json

# Git ì „ì—­ ì„¤ì •(ìœˆë„ìš° ì‘ì—… ë””ë ‰í† ë¦¬ CRLF)
git config core.autocrlf true

# ì† ì‹œì›íˆ í•œ ë²ˆ ì¬ì²´í¬

ì´ê±¸ë¡œ CRLF/LF ê²½ê³  ëŒ€ë¶€ë¶„ ì‚¬ë¼ì§„ë‹¤. ì´ë¯¸ ì²´í¬ì•„ì›ƒëœ íŒŒì¼ ì¤‘ ì¶©ëŒë‚˜ëŠ” ê±´ ë‹¤ìŒ ì»¤ë°‹ì—ì„œ ì •ë¦¬ëœë‹¤.

2) autofix.ps1 ì—…ë°ì´íŠ¸: â€œì»¤ë°‹ ê°€ëŠ¥í•œ íŒŒì¼ë§Œâ€ ì»¤ë°‹, ì‹œí¬ë¦¿/ë°±ì—…ì€ ë¬´ì‹œ

ì§€ê¸ˆ ë¬´í•œ ë°˜ë³µ ì›ì¸ì€ ì»¤ë°‹ ëŒ€ìƒì— ì‹œí¬ë¦¿/ë°±ì—… íŒŒì¼ì´ ë¼ì–´ìˆê¸° ë•Œë¬¸.
ì•„ë˜ ê°œì„ ë³¸ì€ ë³€ê²½ íŒŒì¼ ëª©ë¡ì„ ë½‘ì•„ì„œ í—ˆìš© íŒ¨í„´ë§Œ ì»¤ë°‹í•œë‹¤.

# C:\giwanos\tools\autofix.ps1 êµì²´
Set-Content -Path "C:\giwanos\tools\autofix.ps1" -Encoding UTF8 -Value @'
param([switch]$Once)

$ErrorActionPreference = "Stop"

function Run-Tests {
    Write-Host "[autofix] pytest ì‹¤í–‰" -ForegroundColor Cyan
    $out = (& python -m pytest -q 2>&1) | Out-String
    $code = $LASTEXITCODE
    return @{ code = $code; log = $out }
}

function Have-CursorAgent {
    try { Get-Command cursor-agent -ErrorAction Stop | Out-Null; return $true } catch { return $false }
}

function Minimal-Fix([string]$log, [string]$diff) {
    if (-not (Have-CursorAgent)) {
        Write-Host "[autofix] cursor-agent ì—†ìŒ. ìë™ìˆ˜ì • ìŠ¤í‚µ" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow
        return
    }
    $prompt = @"
í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ì‹¤íŒ¨ë¥¼ ìµœì†Œ ìˆ˜ì •ìœ¼ë¡œ ê³ ì³ë¼.
ê·œì¹™: VELOS ê²½ë¡œëŠ” í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ ê¸°ë°˜(ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ê¸ˆì§€), ë³€ê²½ì€ í•„ìš”í•œ ë¶€ë¶„ë§Œ.
í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ë¡œê·¸:
$log

Diff(ê¸°ì¤€):
$diff
"@
    cursor-agent -p $prompt --print | Out-Null
}

function Get-ChangedFiles {
    $lines = (git status --porcelain) -split "`n" | ForEach-Object { $_.Trim() } | Where-Object { $_ }
    $files = @()
    foreach ($l in $lines) {
        # í¬ë§·: "XY path" ë˜ëŠ” "XY path -> path2"
        $p = $l -replace '^\S+\s+', ''
        if ($p -like '* -> *') { $p = $p.Split('>')[-1].Trim() }
        $files += $p
    }
    return $files
}

# í—ˆìš© íŒ¨í„´(ì´ì™¸ëŠ” ì»¤ë°‹ ì•ˆ í•¨)
$ALLOW = @(
    '*.py','*.ps1','*.md','*.json','*.yaml','*.yml'
)

# ì°¨ë‹¨ íŒ¨í„´
$BLOCK = @(
    'configs/.env',
    'data/backups/*',
    'data/reports/_dispatch/_failed/*',
    'data/reports/_dispatch_processed/*'
)

function Should-Commit {
    $files = Get-ChangedFiles
    if (-not $files -or $files.Count -eq 0) { return $false }

    # ë¸”ë¡ ëª©ë¡ì— ê±¸ë¦¬ë©´ ì œì™¸
    $effective = @()
    foreach ($f in $files) {
        $blocked = $false
        foreach ($b in $BLOCK) { if ([System.Management.Automation.WildcardPattern]::new($b).IsMatch($f)) { $blocked = $true; break } }
        if ($blocked) { continue }

        $allowed = $false
        foreach ($a in $ALLOW) { if ([System.Management.Automation.WildcardPattern]::new($a).IsMatch($f)) { $allowed = $true; break } }
        if ($allowed) { $effective += $f }
    }

    if ($effective.Count -eq 0) {
        if ($files.Count -gt 0) {
            Write-Host "ğŸš« Path blocked (secrets/backup or not allowed):" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow
            $files | ForEach-Object { Write-Host "  - $_" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow }
        }
        return $false
    }

    # ìŠ¤í…Œì´ì§€ì— ì˜¬ë¦¬ê¸°
    foreach ($f in $effective) { git add -- $f | Out-Null }
    return $true
}

function Commit-If-Allowed {
    if (Should-Commit) {
        try {
            git -c user.email=ci@local -c user.name=ci commit -m "autofix: minimal patch via Cursor agent" | Out-Null
            Write-Host "[autofix] ë³€ê²½ ì»¤ë°‹" -ForegroundColor Green
        } catch {
            Write-Host "[autofix] ì»¤ë°‹ ì‹¤íŒ¨: $($_.Exception.Message)" -ForegroundColor Red
        }
    } else {
        Write-Host "[autofix] ì»¤ë°‹í•  ìœ íš¨ ë³€ê²½ ì—†ìŒ" -ForegroundColor DarkGray
    }
}

function Run-Once {
    $t = Run-Tests
    if ($t.code -ne 0) {
        $diff = (git diff --unified=0) | Out-String
        Minimal-Fix -log $t.log -diff $diff
        Commit-If-Allowed
    } else {
        Write-Host "[autofix] í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ í†µê³¼" -ForegroundColor Green
    }
}

if ($Once) {
    Run-Once
    exit 0
}

Write-Host "[autofix] íŒŒì¼ ë³€ê²½ ê°ì‹œ ì‹œì‘ (3ì´ˆ ê°„ê²©)" -ForegroundColor Cyan
while ($true) {
    Start-Sleep 3
    $dirty = (git status --porcelain) | Out-String
    if ($dirty.Trim().Length -gt 0) {
        Run-Once
    }
}
'@

3) ì¬ì‹¤í–‰

1) velos-run.ps1 ìˆ˜ì •: -Once ìŠ¤ìœ„ì¹˜ ê°•ì œ ì „ë‹¬

Set-Content -Path "C:\giwanos\tools\velos-run.ps1" -Encoding UTF8 -Value @'
param([switch]$Once)

$pwsh = "C:\Program Files\PowerShell\7\pwsh.exe"
$ps   = "$env:SystemRoot\System32\WindowsPowerShell\v1.0\powershell.exe"

function Run-PowerShellFile([string]$file,[string[]]$args) {
    if (Test-Path $pwsh) {
        & $pwsh -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File $file @args
    } else {
        & $ps   -NoProfile -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File $file @args
    }
}

# 1. ë©”ëª¨ë¦¬ í—¬ìŠ¤ì²´í¬

2) autofix.ps1 ìˆ˜ì •: ì‚­ì œ/ë¦¬ë„¤ì„ ì•ˆì „ ìŠ¤í…Œì´ì§• + í—ˆìš©/ì°¨ë‹¨ í•„í„°

ì§€ê¸ˆì²˜ëŸ¼ â€œì—†ëŠ” íŒŒì¼ì— addâ€í•˜ë‹ˆ pathspec í„°ì§„ë‹¤.
ìƒíƒœë³„ë¡œ git add/git rm ë‚˜ëˆ ì„œ ì²˜ë¦¬í•œë‹¤.

Set-Content -Path "C:\giwanos\tools\autofix.ps1" -Encoding UTF8 -Value @'
param([switch]$Once)
$ErrorActionPreference = "Stop"

function Run-Tests {
    Write-Host "[autofix] pytest ì‹¤í–‰" -ForegroundColor Cyan
    $out = (& python -m pytest -q 2>&1) | Out-String
    $code = $LASTEXITCODE
    return @{ code = $code; log = $out }
}

function Have-CursorAgent {
    try { Get-Command cursor-agent -ErrorAction Stop | Out-Null; return $true } catch { return $false }
}

function Minimal-Fix([string]$log, [string]$diff) {
    if (-not (Have-CursorAgent)) {
        Write-Host "[autofix] cursor-agent ì—†ìŒ. ìë™ìˆ˜ì • ìŠ¤í‚µ" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow
        return
    }
    $prompt = @"
í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ì‹¤íŒ¨ë¥¼ ìµœì†Œ ìˆ˜ì •ìœ¼ë¡œ ê³ ì³ë¼.
ê·œì¹™: VELOS ê²½ë¡œëŠ” í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ ê¸°ë°˜(ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ê¸ˆì§€), ë³€ê²½ì€ í•„ìš”í•œ ë¶€ë¶„ë§Œ.
í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ ë¡œê·¸:
$log

Diff(ê¸°ì¤€):
$diff
"@
    cursor-agent -p $prompt --print | Out-Null
}

# í—ˆìš©/ì°¨ë‹¨ íŒ¨í„´
$ALLOW = @('*.py','*.ps1','*.md','*.json','*.yaml','*.yml')
$BLOCK = @('configs/.env','data/backups/*','data/reports/_dispatch/_failed/*','data/reports/_dispatch_processed/*')

function Match-Any($path, $patterns) {
    foreach ($p in $patterns) {
        if ([System.Management.Automation.WildcardPattern]::new($p,[System.Management.Automation.WildcardOptions]::IgnoreCase).IsMatch($path)) { return $true }
    }
    return $false
}

# porcelain íŒŒì‹±: XY status + ê²½ë¡œ (ë¦¬ë„¤ì„ì€ old -> new)
function Get-Changes {
    $lines = git status --porcelain | ForEach-Object { $_.TrimEnd() } | Where-Object { $_ }
    $out = @()
    foreach ($l in $lines) {
        if ($l -match '^(?<st>.{2})\s+(?<rest>.+)$') {
            $st = $Matches.st
            $rest = $Matches.rest
            $old = $null; $new = $rest
            if ($rest -like '* -> *') {
                $parts = $rest -split '\s+->\s+'
                $old = $parts[0]; $new = $parts[1]
            }
            $obj = [pscustomobject]@{ Status=$st; Old=$old; Path=$new }
            $out += $obj
        }
    }
    return $out
}

function Stage-Allowed {
    $changes = Get-Changes
    if (-not $changes -or $changes.Count -eq 0) { return $false }

    $stagedSomething = $false
    $blocked = @()

    foreach ($c in $changes) {
        $p = $c.Path
        $o = $c.Old

        # ì°¨ë‹¨ ê²½ë¡œ ì œì™¸
        if (Match-Any $p $BLOCK -or ($o -and (Match-Any $o $BLOCK))) {
            $blocked += $p
            continue
        }
        # í—ˆìš© í™•ì¥ìë§Œ ì²˜ë¦¬
        if (-not (Match-Any $p $ALLOW) -and -not ($o -and (Match-Any $o $ALLOW))) { continue }

        $X = $c.Status.Substring(0,1)
        $Y = $c.Status.Substring(1,1)

        # ì‚­ì œ ì²˜ë¦¬: íŒŒì¼ì´ ë¬¼ë¦¬ì ìœ¼ë¡œ ì—†ìœ¼ë©´ rm, ìˆìœ¼ë©´ add
        if ($X -eq 'D' -or $Y -eq 'D') {
            git rm --quiet --ignore-unmatch -- $p 2>$null
            if ($o) { git rm --quiet --ignore-unmatch -- $o 2>$null }
            $stagedSomething = $true
            continue
        }

        # ë¦¬ë„¤ì„/ë³€ê²½: êµ¬ê²½ë¡œ ì œê±° í›„ ì‹ ê²½ë¡œ ì¶”ê°€
        if ($X -eq 'R' -or $Y -eq 'R' -or $o) {
            if ($o) { git rm --quiet --ignore-unmatch -- $o 2>$null }
            if (Test-Path $p) { git add -- $p | Out-Null }
            $stagedSomething = $true
            continue
        }

        # ê·¸ ì™¸ ë³€ê²½: ì¡´ì¬í•˜ë©´ add
        if (Test-Path $p) {
            git add -- $p | Out-Null
            $stagedSomething = $true
        }
    }

    if ($blocked.Count -gt 0) {
        Write-Host "ğŸš« Path blocked (secrets/backup):" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow
        $blocked | Sort-Object -Unique | ForEach-Object { Write-Host "  - $_" -ForegroundColor DarkYellow }
    }
    return $stagedSomething
}

function Commit-If-Allowed {
    if (Stage-Allowed) {
        try {
            git -c user.email=ci@local -c user.name=ci commit -m "autofix: minimal patch via Cursor agent" | Out-Null
            Write-Host "[autofix] ë³€ê²½ ì»¤ë°‹" -ForegroundColor Green
        } catch {
            Write-Host "[autofix] ì»¤ë°‹ ì‹¤íŒ¨: $($_.Exception.Message)" -ForegroundColor Red
        }
    } else {
        Write-Host "[autofix] ì»¤ë°‹í•  ìœ íš¨ ë³€ê²½ ì—†ìŒ" -ForegroundColor DarkGray
    }
}

function Run-Once {
    $t = Run-Tests
    if ($t.code -ne 0) {
        $diff = (git diff --unified=0) | Out-String
        Minimal-Fix -log $t.log -diff $diff
        Commit-If-Allowed
    } else {
        Write-Host "[autofix] í…ŒìŠ¤íŠ¸ í†µê³¼" -ForegroundColor Green
    }
}

if ($Once) { Run-Once; exit 0 }

Write-Host "[autofix] íŒŒì¼ ë³€ê²½ ê°ì‹œ ì‹œì‘ (3ì´ˆ ê°„ê²©)" -ForegroundColor Cyan
while ($true) {
    Start-Sleep 3
    $dirty = (git status --porcelain) | Out-String
    if ($dirty.Trim().Length -gt 0) { Run-Once }
}
'@

function Add-UserPathOnce([string]$dir) {
  $cur = [Environment]::GetEnvironmentVariable("Path","User")
  $parts = ($cur -split ';') | Where-Object { $_ -and ($_ -ne $dir) }
  $new = ($parts + $dir) -join ';'
  [Environment]::SetEnvironmentVariable("Path",$new,"User")
}

# scripts/run_giwanos_master_loop.py
# GIWANOS: ì‹¤í–‰í™˜ê²½ ì •ë¹„ + ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸ + (ì˜µì…˜) ìƒ˜í”Œ ë””ìŠ¤íŒ¨ì¹˜
import os
import json
import subprocess
from datetime import datetime
from pathlib import Path
from typing import List, Tuple, Optional

# ----------------------------
# ê¸°ë³¸ ì„¤ì • (ì ˆëŒ€ê²½ë¡œ ê¸ˆì§€)
# ----------------------------
def get_root() -> Path:
    root = os.getenv("VELOS_ROOT")
    if not root:
        raise EnvironmentError("í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ VELOS_ROOTê°€ ì„¤ì •ë˜ì§€ ì•Šì•˜ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ì˜ˆ: setx VELOS_ROOT C:\\giwanos /M")
    p = Path(root)
    if not p.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"VELOS_ROOT ê²½ë¡œê°€ ì—†ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤: {p}")
    return p.resolve()

ROOT = get_root()
DOCS = ROOT / "docs"
DATA = ROOT / "data"
CONFIGS = ROOT / "configs"
TOOLS = ROOT / "tools"
SCRIPTS = ROOT / "scripts"
MODULES = ROOT / "modules"

REQUIRED_DIRS = [DOCS, DATA, CONFIGS, TOOLS, SCRIPTS, MODULES]
ESSENTIAL_FILES = {
    CONFIGS / ".env": "# GIWANOS dotenv (í•„ìš” í‚¤ë¥¼ ì—¬ê¸°ì— ì¶”ê°€)\nVELOS_ENV=dev\n",
}

DISPATCH_OUT = DATA / "dispatch" / "_queue"
REPORT_PATH = DOCS / "CONTEXT_PACK.md"
TASK_NAME = "VELOS-Autofix-Once-At-Logon"

# ----------------------------
# ìœ í‹¸
# ----------------------------
def run(cmd: List[str], cwd: Optional[Path] = None, timeout: int = 15) -> Tuple[int, str]:
    try:
        p = subprocess.run(
            cmd, cwd=str(cwd) if cwd else None,
            stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.STDOUT,
            text=True, timeout=timeout, shell=False
        )
        return p.returncode, p.stdout.strip()
    except Exception as e:
        return 999, f"[EXCEPTION] {e}"

def yes_no(flag: bool) -> str:
    return "âœ…" if flag else "âŒ"

def ensure_dirs_and_files() -> List[str]:
    notes = []
    for d in REQUIRED_DIRS:
        if not d.exists():
            d.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
            notes.append(f"ğŸ“ í´ë” ìƒì„±: {d.relative_to(ROOT)}")
        else:
            notes.append(f"ğŸ“ í´ë” í™•ì¸: {d.relative_to(ROOT)}")

    for f, content in ESSENTIAL_FILES.items():
        if not f.exists():
            f.write_text(content, encoding="utf-8")
            notes.append(f"ğŸ§¾ í…œí”Œë¦¿ ìƒì„±: {f.relative_to(ROOT)}")
        else:
            notes.append(f"ğŸ§¾ íŒŒì¼ í™•ì¸: {f.relative_to(ROOT)}")
    return notes

def git_status() -> List[str]:
    notes = []
    # ë£¨íŠ¸ê°€ git ì €ì¥ì†Œì¸ì§€
    code, out = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--is-inside-work-tree"], cwd=ROOT)
    if code != 0 or out.strip().lower() != "true":
        notes.append("âŒ Git: í˜„ì¬ í´ë”ê°€ ì €ì¥ì†Œë¡œ ì¸ì‹ë˜ì§€ ì•ŠìŒ (.git ëˆ„ë½ ë˜ëŠ” ìµœìƒìœ„ê°€ ì•„ë‹˜)")
        return notes

    notes.append("âœ… Git: ì €ì¥ì†Œ ì¸ì‹ OK")

    # ìµœìƒìœ„ ê²½ë¡œ
    _, top = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--show-toplevel"], cwd=ROOT)
    notes.append(f"â€¢ repo-top: {top}")

    # ë¸Œëœì¹˜/ì»¤ë°‹
    _, br = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--abbrev-ref", "HEAD"], cwd=ROOT)
    _, sha = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--short", "HEAD"], cwd=ROOT)
    notes.append(f"â€¢ branch: {br} @ {sha}")

    # ì›ê²©
    _, rem = run(["git", "remote", "-v"], cwd=ROOT)
    if rem.strip():
        notes.append("â€¢ remotes:\n" + "\n".join(["  " + l for l in rem.splitlines()]))
    else:
        notes.append("â€¢ remotes: (ì—†ìŒ)")

    # ë³€ê²½ì‚¬í•­
    _, dirty = run(["git", "status", "--porcelain"], cwd=ROOT)
    if dirty.strip():
        notes.append("â€¢ ë³€ê²½ì‚¬í•­ ì¡´ì¬:\n" + "\n".join(["  " + l for l in dirty.splitlines()]))
    else:
        notes.append("â€¢ ì‘ì—…íŠ¸ë¦¬ ê¹¨ë—í•¨")
    return notes

def query_task(name: str) -> List[str]:
    notes = []
    code, out = run(["schtasks", "/Query", "/TN", name])
    if code != 0:
        notes.append(f"âŒ ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ëŸ¬ íƒœìŠ¤í¬ ì—†ìŒ: {name}")
        return notes

    notes.append(f"âœ… ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ëŸ¬ íƒœìŠ¤í¬ ì¡´ì¬: {name}")
    # ë§ˆì§€ë§‰ ì‹¤í–‰ ê²°ê³¼ í™•ì¸
    _, detail = run(["schtasks", "/Query", "/TN", name, "/V", "/FO", "LIST"])
    notes.append("â€¢ ìƒì„¸:\n" + "\n".join(["  " + l for l in detail.splitlines()[:30]]))  # ë„ˆë¬´ ê¸¸ë©´ 30ì¤„ë§Œ
    return notes

def write_report(sections: List[Tuple[str, List[str]]]) -> Path:
    lines = []
    ts = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
    lines.append(f"# GIWANOS ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸")
    lines.append(f"- ìƒì„±ì‹œê°: {ts}")
    lines.append(f"- ROOT: `{ROOT}`")
    lines.append("")

    for title, items in sections:
        lines.append(f"## {title}")
        if not items:
            lines.append("- (ë‚´ìš© ì—†ìŒ)")
        else:
            for it in items:
                # í‘œê°€ ì•„ë‹Œ ì¼ë°˜ ëª©ë¡(í”„ë¡¬í”„íŠ¸ ì •ì±… ì¤€ìˆ˜: ê¸´ ë¬¸ì¥ í‘œ ê¸ˆì§€)
                lines.append(f"- {it}")
        lines.append("")

    REPORT_PATH.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    REPORT_PATH.write_text("\n".join(lines), encoding="utf-8")
    return REPORT_PATH

def make_sample_dispatch() -> Path:
    q = DISPATCH_OUT
    q.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    payload = {
        "ticket_id": f"manual_{datetime.now().strftime('%Y%m%d_%H%M%S')}",
        "created_at": datetime.now().isoformat(timespec="seconds"),
        "type": "sample",
        "message": "ìƒ˜í”Œ ë””ìŠ¤íŒ¨ì¹˜ í‹°ì¼“(ìˆ˜ë™ ìƒì„±)",
    }
    out = q / f"{payload['ticket_id']}.json"
    out.write_text(json.dumps(payload, ensure_ascii=False, indent=2), encoding="utf-8")
    return out

# ----------------------------
# ë©”ì¸
# ----------------------------
def main():
    sections = []

    # 1) í´ë”/íŒŒì¼ ë³´ì¥
    notes_fs = ensure_dirs_and_files()
    sections.append(("íŒŒì¼ì‹œìŠ¤í…œ ì ê²€", notes_fs))

    # 2) Git ìƒíƒœ
    sections.append(("Git ìƒíƒœ", git_status()))

    # 3) ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ëŸ¬ íƒœìŠ¤í¬
    sections.append(("ìë™ì‹¤í–‰ íƒœìŠ¤í¬", query_task(TASK_NAME)))

    # 4) Python / PowerShell ë²„ì „ í‘œê¸°

    ps7 = os.getenv("PSModulePath") is not None  # ë‹¨ìˆœ í”Œë˜ê·¸ ëŠë‚Œ
    sections.append(("ëŸ°íƒ€ì„", [py_ver, f"í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ PSModulePath ì¡´ì¬: {yes_no(ps7)}"]))

    # 5) (ì˜µì…˜) ìƒ˜í”Œ ë””ìŠ¤íŒ¨ì¹˜ ë°œí–‰
    try:
        p = make_sample_dispatch()
        sections.append(("ë””ìŠ¤íŒ¨ì¹˜", [f"ìƒ˜í”Œ í‹°ì¼“ ìƒì„±: {p.relative_to(ROOT)}"]))
    except Exception as e:
        sections.append(("ë””ìŠ¤íŒ¨ì¹˜", [f"âŒ ìƒì„± ì‹¤íŒ¨: {e}"]))

    # ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸ ì“°ê¸°
    out = write_report(sections)
    print(f"âœ… ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸ ìƒì„±: {out}")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()

# scripts/run_giwanos_master_loop.py
# GIWANOS: ì‹¤í–‰í™˜ê²½ ì •ë¹„ + ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸ + Slack/Email ì „ì†¡
import os
import json
import smtplib
import requests
import subprocess
from datetime import datetime
from pathlib import Path
from typing import List, Tuple, Optional
from email.mime.base import MIMEBase
from email.mime.multipart import MIMEMultipart
from email.mime.text import MIMEText
from email import encoders

# ----------------------------
# í™˜ê²½ ë³€ìˆ˜ ë° ê²½ë¡œ
# ----------------------------
def get_root() -> Path:
    root = os.getenv("VELOS_ROOT")
    if not root:
        raise EnvironmentError("í™˜ê²½ë³€ìˆ˜ VELOS_ROOTê°€ ì„¤ì •ë˜ì§€ ì•Šì•˜ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤.")
    p = Path(root)
    if not p.exists():
        raise FileNotFoundError(f"VELOS_ROOT ê²½ë¡œê°€ ì—†ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤: {p}")
    return p.resolve()

ROOT = get_root()
DOCS = ROOT / "docs"
DATA = ROOT / "data"
CONFIGS = ROOT / "configs"
TOOLS = ROOT / "tools"
SCRIPTS = ROOT / "scripts"
MODULES = ROOT / "modules"

REQUIRED_DIRS = [DOCS, DATA, CONFIGS, TOOLS, SCRIPTS, MODULES]
ESSENTIAL_FILES = {
    CONFIGS / ".env": "# GIWANOS dotenv\nVELOS_ENV=dev\n"
}
DISPATCH_OUT = DATA / "dispatch" / "_queue"
REPORT_PATH = DOCS / "CONTEXT_PACK.md"
TASK_NAME = "VELOS-Autofix-Once-At-Logon"

# ----------------------------
# ìœ í‹¸ í•¨ìˆ˜
# ----------------------------
def run(cmd: List[str], cwd: Optional[Path] = None, timeout: int = 15) -> Tuple[int, str]:
    try:
        p = subprocess.run(
            cmd, cwd=str(cwd) if cwd else None,
            stdout=subprocess.PIPE, stderr=subprocess.STDOUT,
            text=True, timeout=timeout, shell=False
        )
        return p.returncode, p.stdout.strip()
    except Exception as e:
        return 999, f"[EXCEPTION] {e}"

def yes_no(flag: bool) -> str:
    return "âœ…" if flag else "âŒ"

def ensure_dirs_and_files() -> List[str]:
    notes = []
    for d in REQUIRED_DIRS:
        if not d.exists():
            d.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
            notes.append(f"ğŸ“ í´ë” ìƒì„±: {d.relative_to(ROOT)}")
        else:
            notes.append(f"ğŸ“ í´ë” í™•ì¸: {d.relative_to(ROOT)}")
    for f, content in ESSENTIAL_FILES.items():
        if not f.exists():
            f.write_text(content, encoding="utf-8")
            notes.append(f"ğŸ§¾ í…œí”Œë¦¿ ìƒì„±: {f.relative_to(ROOT)}")
        else:
            notes.append(f"ğŸ§¾ íŒŒì¼ í™•ì¸: {f.relative_to(ROOT)}")
    return notes

def git_status() -> List[str]:
    notes = []
    code, out = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--is-inside-work-tree"], cwd=ROOT)
    if code != 0 or out.strip().lower() != "true":
        notes.append("âŒ Git ì €ì¥ì†Œ ì•„ë‹˜")
        return notes
    notes.append("âœ… Git ì €ì¥ì†Œ OK")
    _, br = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--abbrev-ref", "HEAD"], cwd=ROOT)
    _, sha = run(["git", "rev-parse", "--short", "HEAD"], cwd=ROOT)
    notes.append(f"â€¢ branch: {br} @ {sha}")
    return notes

def query_task(name: str) -> List[str]:
    notes = []
    code, _ = run(["schtasks", "/Query", "/TN", name])
    if code != 0:
        notes.append(f"âŒ ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ëŸ¬ íƒœìŠ¤í¬ ì—†ìŒ: {name}")
    else:
        notes.append(f"âœ… ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¤„ëŸ¬ íƒœìŠ¤í¬ ì¡´ì¬: {name}")
    return notes

def write_report(sections: List[Tuple[str, List[str]]]) -> Path:
    ts = datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S")
    lines = [f"# GIWANOS ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸", f"- ìƒì„±ì‹œê°: {ts}", f"- ROOT: `{ROOT}`", ""]
    for title, items in sections:
        lines.append(f"## {title}")
        for it in items:
            lines.append(f"- {it}")
        lines.append("")
    REPORT_PATH.parent.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
    REPORT_PATH.write_text("\n".join(lines), encoding="utf-8")
    return REPORT_PATH

# ----------------------------
# Slack & Email
# ----------------------------
def load_env() -> dict:
    env_file = CONFIGS / ".env"
    if not env_file.exists():
        return {}
    env = {}
    for line in env_file.read_text(encoding="utf-8").splitlines():
        if "=" in line and not line.strip().startswith("#"):
            k, v = line.split("=", 1)
            env[k.strip()] = v.strip()
    return env

def send_slack(webhook_url: str, text: str):
    try:
        res = requests.post(webhook_url, json={"text": text}, timeout=10)
        if res.status_code != 200:
            print(f"[Slack] ì „ì†¡ ì‹¤íŒ¨: {res.status_code} {res.text}")
        else:
            print("[Slack] ì „ì†¡ ì™„ë£Œ")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[Slack] ì˜ˆì™¸: {e}")

def send_email(env: dict, subject: str, body: str, attachment: Path):
    try:
        msg = MIMEMultipart()
        msg["From"] = env.get("SMTP_USER")
        msg["To"] = env.get("SMTP_TO")
        msg["Subject"] = subject
        msg.attach(MIMEText(body, "plain", "utf-8"))

        with open(attachment, "rb") as f:
            part = MIMEBase("application", "octet-stream")
            part.set_payload(f.read())
            encoders.encode_base64(part)
            part.add_header("Content-Disposition", f"attachment; filename={attachment.name}")
            msg.attach(part)

        with smtplib.SMTP(env.get("SMTP_HOST"), int(env.get("SMTP_PORT", 587))) as server:
            server.starttls()
            server.login(env.get("SMTP_USER"), env.get("SMTP_PASS"))
            server.send_message(msg)
        print("[Email] ì „ì†¡ ì™„ë£Œ")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"[Email] ì˜ˆì™¸: {e}")

# ----------------------------
# ë©”ì¸
# ----------------------------
def main():
    sections = []
    sections.append(("íŒŒì¼ì‹œìŠ¤í…œ ì ê²€", ensure_dirs_and_files()))
    sections.append(("Git ìƒíƒœ", git_status()))
    sections.append(("ìë™ì‹¤í–‰ íƒœìŠ¤í¬", query_task(TASK_NAME)))

    out = write_report(sections)
    print(f"âœ… ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸ ìƒì„±: {out}")

    env = load_env()
    slack_url = env.get("SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL")
    if slack_url:
        send_slack(slack_url, f"VELOS ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸ ìƒì„±ë¨: {out}")

    if env.get("SMTP_HOST"):
        send_email(env, "VELOS ìƒíƒœ ë¦¬í¬íŠ¸", "ì²¨ë¶€ ì°¸ì¡°", out)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
